nRhiJb-ObfsIf nRhiJb-fmcmS-oXtfBe"><div class="nRhiJb-kR0ZEf-OWXEXe-GV1x9e-c5RTEf"></div><div class="nRhiJb-kR0ZEf-OWXEXe-GV1x9e-qWD73c"><h5 class="cHE8Ub Qwf2Db-MnozTc Qwf2Db-MnozTc-OWXEXe-MnozTc-qWD73c">Mandiant </h5><p class="nRhiJb-qJTHM khCp7b"></p></div></section></div></section><div class="nRhiJb-DARUcf"><div class="nRhiJb-ObfsIf nRhiJb-DbgRPb-wNfPc-ma6Yeb nRhiJb-DbgRPb-qWD73c-cGMI2b"><div class="nRhiJb-kR0ZEf-OWXEXe-GV1x9e-ibL1re dzoHJ"></div><div class="OYL9D nRhiJb-kR0ZEf-OWXEXe-GV1x9e-OiUrBf" jsname="tx2NYc"><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Written by: <span style="vertical-align:baseline">Ofir Rozmann, Asli Koksal, Adrian Hernandez, Sarah Bock, Jonathan Leathery</span></p>
<hr>
<p> </p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p style="text-align:left"><a href="https://cloud.google.com/blog/topics/threat-intelligence/apt42-charms-cons-compromises" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">APT42</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, an Iranian state-sponsored cyber espionage actor, is using enhanced social engineering schemes to gain access to victim networks, including cloud environments. The actor is targeting Western and Middle Eastern NGOs, media organizations, academia, legal services and activists. Mandiant assesses APT42 operates on behalf of the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps Intelligence Organization (IRGC-IO).</span></p>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">APT42 was observed posing as journalists and event organizers to build trust with their victims through ongoing correspondence, and to deliver invitations to conferences or legitimate documents. These social engineering schemes enabled APT42 to harvest credentials and use them to gain initial access to cloud environments. Subsequently, the threat actor covertly exfiltrated data of strategic interest to Iran, while relying on built-in features and open-source tools to avoid detection.</span></p>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">In addition to cloud operations, we also outline recent malware-based APT42 operations using two custom backdoors: NICECURL and TAMECAT. These backdoors are delivered via spear phishing, providing the attackers with initial access that might be used as a command execution interface or as a jumping point to deploy additional malware</span><span style="vertical-align:baseline">.</span></p>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">APT42 targeting and missions are consistent with its assessed affiliation with the IRGC-IO, which is a part of the Iranian intelligence apparatus that is responsible for monitoring and preventing foreign threats to the Islamic Republic and domestic unrest.</span></p>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">APT42 activities overlap with the publicly reported actors CALANQUE (Google Threat Analysis Group), </span><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Charming Kitten (</span><a href="https://www.clearskysec.com/the-kittens-are-back-in-town-3/" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">ClearSky</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> and </span><a href="https://blog.certfa.com/posts/fake-interview-the-new-activity-of-charming-kitten/" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">CERTFA</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline">), Mint Sandstorm/Phosphorus (</span><a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/security/blog/2023/04/18/nation-state-threat-actor-mint-sandstorm-refines-tradecraft-to-attack-high-value-targets/" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">Microsoft</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline">), TA453 (</span><a href="https://www.proofpoint.com/us/blog/threat-insight/badblood-ta453-targets-us-and-israeli-medical-research-personnel-credential" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">Proofpoint</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline">), Yellow Garuda (</span><a href="https://www.pwc.com/gx/en/issues/cybersecurity/cyber-threat-intelligence/old-cat-new-tricks.html" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">PwC</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline">), and ITG18 (</span><a href="https://securityintelligence.com/posts/new-research-exposes-iranian-threat-group-operations/" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">IBM X-Force</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline">).</span></p></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig1.max-700x700.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig1.max-700x700.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig1.max-700x700.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig1.max-700x700.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Figure 1: APT42 operations</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><h2 style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Fake News, Real Credentials: Harvesting Microsoft, Yahoo, and Google Credentials</span></h2>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">APT42 is known for its extensive credential harvesting operations that are often accompanied by tailored spear-phishing campaigns and extensive social engineering. APT42 credential harvesting operations typically include three steps, described in the Figure 2.</span></p></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig2.max-1600x1600.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig2.max-1600x1600.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig2.max-1600x1600.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig2.max-1600x1600.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Figure 2: APT42 credential harvesting campaign attack lifecycle</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Mandiant identified at least three clusters of infrastructure used by APT42 to harvest credentials from targets in the policy and government sectors, media organizations and journalists, and NGOs and activists. The three clusters employ similar tactics, techniques and procedures (TTPs) to target victim credentials (spear-phishing emails), but use slightly varied domains, masquerading patterns, decoys, and themes.</span></p>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">A full list of the infrastructure is available in the Indicators of Compromise (IOCs) section.</span></p>
<h4 style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Cluster A: Posing as News Outlets and NGOs</span></h4>
<ul>
<li style="text-align:left"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Active:</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> 2021 – today</span></li>
<li style="text-align:left"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Suspected Targeting:</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> credentials of journalists, researchers, and geopolitical entities in regions of interest to Iran. </span></li>
<li style="text-align:left"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Masquerading as:</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> The Washington Post (U.S.), The Economist (UK), The Jerusalem Post (IL), Khaleej Times (UAE), Azadliq (Azerbaijan), and more news outlets and NGOs. This often involves the use of typosquatted domains like washin</span><strong style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">q</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">tonpost[.]press. <br></span><br>Mandiant did not observe APT42 target or compromise these organizations, but rather impersonate them.</li>
<li style="text-align:left"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Attack vector:</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> Malicious links from typo-squatted domains that are masquerading as news articles likely sent via spear phishing, redirecting the user to fake Google login pages.</span></li>
</ul></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig3.max-800x800.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig3.max-800x800.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig3.max-800x800.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig3.max-800x800.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Figure 3: Jerusalem Post journalist warns of spear-phishing emails sent on her behalf</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><h4 style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Cluster B: Posing as Legitimate Services</span></h4>
<ul style="text-align:left">
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p style="text-align:justify"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Active:</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> 2019 – today</span></p>
</li>
</ul>
<ul style="text-align:left">
<li style="list-style-type:disc;vertical-align:baseline">
<p style="text-align:justify"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Targeting:</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> individuals perceived as a threat to the Iranian regime, including researchers, journalists, NGO leaders, and human rights activists.</span></p>
</li>
<li style="text-align:justify"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Masquerading as:</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> generic login pages, file hosting services, and YouTube. The domains use TLDs like .top, .online, .site and .live, and often contain several words separated by hyphens, like panel-live-check[.]online.</span></li>
<li style="text-align:justify"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Attack vector:</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> legitimate links sent via spear phishing, posing as invitations to conferences or legitimate documents hosted on cloud infrastructure. Upon entry, the user is prompted to enter their credentials, which are sent to the attackers.</span></li>
</ul>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Mandiant observed several instances of APT42 using Cluster B domains to harvest credentials and host decoy files:</span></p>
<ul>
<li style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">In March 2023, APT42 deployed the domain ksview[.]top in an attempt to redirect to honest-halcyon-fresher[.]buzz, which hosts a fake Gmail login page targeting a freelance journalist, indicating these campaigns are highly tailored to their targets.</span></li>
</ul></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH H05fDc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig4.max-700x700.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig4.max-700x700.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH H05fDc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig4.max-700x700.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig4.max-700x700.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Figure 4: Fake Gmail login page used by APT42</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><ul>
<li style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">In March 2023, APT42 sent a spear-phishing email with a fake Google Meet invitation, allegedly sent on behalf of Mona Louri, a likely fake persona leveraged by APT42, claiming to be a human rights activist and researcher. Upon entry, the user was presented with a fake Google Meet page and asked to enter their credentials, which were subsequently sent to the attackers.</span></li>
</ul></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig5.max-1000x1000.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig5.max-1000x1000.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig5.max-1000x1000.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig5.max-1000x1000.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Figure 5: Twitter account of Mona Louri, a likely fake persona leveraged by APT42</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><ul>
<li style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The fake page was hosted on Google Sites (sites[.]google[.]com) webpage creation tool to enhance its legitimacy, and had a reference to a dedicated APT42 domain embedded in its HTML contents, as can be observed in Figure 6 and Figure 7. This activity was also </span><a href="https://twitter.com/NarimanGharib/status/1635333465028857856" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">publicly mentioned</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> on Twitter.</span></li>
</ul></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig6.max-1500x1500.png" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Figure 6: Fake Google Meet page deployed by APT42</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig7.max-1000x1000.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Figure 7: APT42 domain embedded in the fake Google Meet page HTML contents</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><ul>
<li style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">From November through December 2023, APT42 targeted the media and non-profit sectors via spear-phishing emails that included the shortened link of the URL shortening service “n9[.]cl,” which redirected victims to a likely credential harvesting page mimicking Google Drive using the domain “review[.]modification-check[.]online” while others included a link to the same domain without the shortener. The actor additionally shared a benign file via Google Drive as part of this campaign.</span></li>
<li style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">In February 2024, Mandiant observed the APT42 domain nterview[.]site redirecting to the domain admin-stable-right[.]top, which hosted a fake Gmail login page, to target the credentials of a women’s rights activist. The domain nterview[.]site was also observed redirecting to a women’s rights-themed lure allegedly sent by “Jamileh Nedai” (possibly referring to the Iranian filmmaker and women’s rights activist). </span>
<ul>
<li style="text-align:left">The lure, named “Questionnaire.pdf,” is a PDF document hosted on Dropbox with the headline “Women’s Struggles and Protest.” The document was created by “David Webb,” possibly referring to the Fox News contributor. We have no indication of this individual being targeted by APT42, but rather being spoofed by them, possibly to enhance the decoy's legitimacy.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig8.max-1000x1000.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig8.max-1000x1000.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig8.max-1000x1000.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig8.max-1000x1000.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Figure 8: APT42 lure shared via Dropbox (left) containing women’s rights-related content (right)</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><ul>
<li style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">In March 2024, APT42 used the domain shortlinkview[.]live, which redirects to panel-view[.]live, in a campaign targeting a news editor working in a Persian-language news television channel. The final redirection hosts a fake Gmail login page.</span></li>
<li style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">During March 2024, APT42 also used the domain reconsider[.]site to redirect users to a decoy document hosted on Dropbox named “The Secrets of Gaza Tunnels” (titled both in Hebrew and in English), likely leveraging the Israel-Hamas war.</span></li>
</ul></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig9.max-1500x1500.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig9.max-1500x1500.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig9.max-1500x1500.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig9.max-1500x1500.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Figure 9: Decoy document titled “The secrets of Gaza Tunnels” used by APT42</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><ul>
<li style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">At the same time, APT42 also used the domain reconsider[.]site to redirect users to last-check-leave[.]buzz and target Google, Microsoft, and Yahoo credentials. This effort was focused on targeting researchers and academia personnel in the U.S., Israel, and Europe.</span></li>
</ul></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig10.max-1200x1200.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig10.max-1200x1200.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig10.max-1200x1200.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig10.max-1200x1200.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Figure 10: Fake Yahoo and Hotmail login page used by APT42</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><ul>
<li style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">In addition, Mandiant also observed APT42 deploy fake YouTube login pages and URL shortener pages, likely disseminated via phishing:</span></li>
</ul></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig11.max-1500x1500.png" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Figure 11: Fake YouTube login page hosted on an APT42 domain</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig12.max-1300x1300.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig12.max-1300x1300.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig12.max-1300x1300.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig12.max-1300x1300.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Figure 12: Fake URL shortener page hosted on multiple APT42 domains</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><h4 style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Cluster C: Posing as “Mailer Daemon,” URL Shortening Services and NGOs</span></h4>
<ul style="text-align:left">
<li style="text-align:justify"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Active:</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> 2022 – today</span></li>
<li style="text-align:justify"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Targeting:</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> individuals and entities affiliated with various defense, foreign affairs, and academic issues in the U.S. and Israel.</span>
<ul>
<li style="text-align:justify"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Specifically, in November 2023, Mandiant observed this cluster targeting a </span><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">nuclear physics professor in a major Israeli university</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, by using the following phishing URL likely masquerading as a legitimate Microsoft 365 login:</span></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="font-style:italic;vertical-align:baseline">hxxps://email-daemon[.]online/</span><strong style="font-style:italic;vertical-align:baseline">&lt;university_acronym&gt;365</strong><span style="font-style:italic;vertical-align:baseline">[.]onmicrosofl[.]com/accountID=</span><strong style="font-style:italic;vertical-align:baseline">&lt;target_handle&gt;</strong></p>
<ul style="text-align:left">
<li style="text-align:justify"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Masquerading as:</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> NGOs, “Mailer Daemon,” and Bitly URL shortening service.</span></li>
<li style="text-align:justify"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Attack vector:</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> legitimate links likely sent via spear phishing, posing as invitations to conferences or legitimate documents hosted on cloud infrastructure. Upon entry, the user is prompted to enter their credentials, which are sent to the attackers.</span></li>
</ul>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">In these cases, Mandiant observed APT42 encode targets or lures using “1337” (</span><span style="font-style:italic;vertical-align:baseline">leet</span><span style="vertical-align:baseline">) writing. For example, the name of Tamir Pardo (the former head of the Israeli Mossad) was represented in the url </span><span style="font-style:italic;vertical-align:baseline">hxxps://bitly[.]org[.]il/</span><strong style="font-style:italic;vertical-align:baseline">t4m1rpa</strong><span style="font-style:italic;vertical-align:baseline"> </span><span style="vertical-align:baseline">by replacing "a" with 4 and "i" with 1.</span></p>
<ul style="text-align:left">
<li style="text-align:justify"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">APT42 likely attempted to use</span><strong style="vertical-align:baseline"> </strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">lures related to the International Counter-Intelligence summit (“ICT-2023”) conducted in Israel, by deploying the following URLs:</span>
<ul>
<li style="text-align:justify"><span style="font-style:italic;text-align:center">hxxps://bitly[.]org[.]il/J03p4y3r</span></li>
<li style="text-align:justify"><span style="font-style:italic;vertical-align:baseline">hxxps://youtransfer[.]live/</span><strong style="font-style:italic;vertical-align:baseline">ICT-2023</strong><span style="font-style:italic;vertical-align:baseline">/J03py3r</span></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h2 style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Head(er) In The Cloud: Targeting Microsoft 365 Environments</span></h2>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">As an extension of their aforementioned credential harvesting operations, during 2022–2023, Mandiant observed APT42 exfiltrate documents of interest to Iran and sensitive information from the victims’ public cloud infrastructure. These victims were located in the U.S. and the UK in the legal services and NGO sectors. However, since the initial enabler of these operations lies with credential harvesting, which APT42 conducts worldwide, it is possible the victimology is much wider.</span></p>
<p style="text-align:left"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">These operations began with enhanced social engineering schemes to gain the initial access to victim networks</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, often involving ongoing trust-building correspondence with the victim. Only then the desired credentials are acquired and multi-factor authentication (MFA) is bypassed, by serving a cloned website to capture the MFA token (which failed) and later by sending MFA push notifications to the victim (which succeeded). </span></p>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">These techniques have allowed APT42 to </span><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">covertly access and compromise the victim’s Microsoft 365 environment</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, relying on built-in features and open-source tools to decrease their chances of being detected.</span></p></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig13.max-1500x1500.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig13.max-1500x1500.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig13.max-1500x1500.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig13.max-1500x1500.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Figure 13: APT42 cloud operations attack lifecycle</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">APT42 cloud operations attack lifecycle can be described in details as follows:</span></p>
<ul>
<li style="text-align:left"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Social engineering schemes involving decoys and trust building, </strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">which includes masquerading as legitimate NGOs and conducting ongoing correspondence with the target, sometimes lasting several weeks. </span>
<ul>
<li style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The threat actor masqueraded as well-known international organizations in the legal and NGO fields and sent emails from domains typosquatting the original NGO domains, for example aspenlnstitute[.]org</span><span style="vertical-align:baseline">. </span>
<ul>
<li style="text-align:justify">The Aspen Institute became aware of this spoofed domain and collaborated with industry partners, including blocking it in SafeBrowsing, thus protecting users of Google Chrome and additional browsers.</li>
<li style="text-align:justify">To increase their credibility, APT42 impersonated high-ranking personnel working at the aforementioned organizations when creating the email personas.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li style="text-align:left">APT42 enhanced their campaign credibility by using decoy material inviting targets to legitimate and relevant events and conferences. In one instance, the decoy material was hosted on an attacker-controlled SharePoint folder, accessible only after the victim entered their credentials. Mandiant did not identify malicious elements in the files, suggesting they were used solely to gain the victim’s trust.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig14.max-900x900.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig14.max-900x900.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig14.max-900x900.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig14.max-900x900.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Figure 14: APT42 controlled SharePoint folder containing PDF lures</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><ul>
<li style="text-align:left"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Credential harvesting and bypassing MFA.</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> Only after a certain level of trust was built with the victim, APT42 harvested the desired credentials by sending the victim a link that would redirect them to a credential harvesting site, similar to the process described in the previously discussed credential theft section. </span>
<ul>
<li style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Mandiant observed the use of Javascript files to redirect victims from these links to ultimately serve fake Microsoft 365 login pages.</span></li>
<li style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">At least once, Mandiant observed APT42 use several methods—both SharePoint login and fake LinkedIn login pages—to target multiple high-profile personnel of the victim organization during the same campaign.</span></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig15.max-600x600.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig15.max-600x600.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig15.max-600x600.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig15.max-600x600.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Figure 15: APT42 fake LinkedIn login page</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><ul>
<li style="list-style-type:none">
<ul>
<li style="text-align:left"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Mandiant observed APT42 deploy two methods to bypass MFA</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">: First, APT42 made attempts to acquire MFA tokens by using fake DUO pages, using subdomains with prefixes such as “api-&lt;generated_id&gt;[.]...” or using words like “duo”. When this failed, the actor sent authentication prompts to victims upon attempts to login, which succeeded. <br><br></span><span style="vertical-align:baseline">In a different intrusion, APT42 likely served a phishing site to capture the MFA token sent via SMS and leveraged the KMSI (Keep-me-Signed-In) feature to avoid reauthentication.</span></li>
<li style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">In at least one instance, APT42 established a “persistent” login mechanism </span><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">leveraging the Microsoft </strong><a href="https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/account-billing/using-app-passwords-with-apps-that-don-t-support-two-step-verification-5896ed9b-4263-e681-128a-a6f2979a7944" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><strong style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">app password</strong></a><strong style="vertical-align:baseline"> feature, likely in attempts to preserve ongoing access for future logins</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> without the need to re-verify their identity with MFA.</span>
<ul>
<li style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Microsoft’s app password feature is intended to be used with applications or devices that do not support MFA, and thus generates single-use passwords that do not require MFA. The feature is not enabled by default, and can be activated manually. Once this feature is enabled, any logged in user can create app passwords.</span></li>
<li style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">APT42 leveraged the fact that the app password feature was enabled to create an app password for the compromised account. However, Mandiant has no indication that APT42 actually used it.</span></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig16.max-500x500.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig16.max-500x500.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig16.max-500x500.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig16.max-500x500.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Figure 16: Microsoft app password settings, exploited by APT42 for continuous MFA bypass</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><ul>
<li style="text-align:left"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Covert exfiltration of data from the Microsoft 365 environment</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, including OneDrive documents, Outlook emails, and documents of potential interest to Iran including files pertaining its foreign affairs or the Persian Gulf region.<br><br></span><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">The M365 infiltration and data exfiltration included the following stages:</strong>
<ul>
<li style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Logging in to the victim email using Thunderbird email client, whose usage was approved by the attacker altering the user permissions.</span></li>
<li style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Logging into the victim’s Citrix application and using Windows Remote Desktop Protocol (RDP). Upon entry, the attackers explored, enumerated, and staged files for exfiltration in password-protected 7-ZIP archives.</span>
<ul>
<li style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The attacker performed host, network, and directory reconnaissance using Windows native commands including:<br><br></span></span>
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">

<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">

</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><ul>
<li style="list-style-type:none">
<ul>
<li style="list-style-type:none">
<ul>
<li style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The attacker used PowerShell cmdlets including "set-ExecutionPolicy," "Import-Module," and "Invoke-HuntSMBShares," a cmdlet from the open-source tooling module </span><a href="https://github.com/NetSPI/PowerHuntShares" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">PowerHuntShares</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> that can identify users with excessive network share permissions.</span></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li style="text-align:left"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Searching for specific files and data of interest to Iran</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">. For example, in one of the intrusions, APT42 searched for specific Iran-related documents with details about foreign affairs issues, as was observed on collected data from the Windows Registry Key HKEY_CURRENT_USER\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Explorer\TypedPaths. In another intrusion, Mandiant observed APT42 browsing for files related to the Middle East as well as the Ukraine war.</span></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig17.max-1800x1800.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig17.max-1800x1800.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig17.max-1800x1800.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig17.max-1800x1800.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Figure 17: APT42 cloud operations flow of attack</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p style="text-align:left"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">APT42 deployed multiple defense evasion techniques</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> to minimize their intrusion footprint:</span></p>
<ul style="text-align:left">
<li style="text-align:justify"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Relying on built-in features of the Microsoft 365 environment and publicly available tools</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">. This serves as double functionality to harden attribution based on tooling and to blend in the environment, while it shows an increase in adaptability.</span></li>
<li style="text-align:justify"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Clearing Google Chrome browser history</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> after reviewing documents of interest.</span></li>
<li style="text-align:justify"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Attempting (and possibly succeeding) to </span><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">exfiltrate files to a OneDrive account masquerading as the victim’s organization</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, using the fake email address &lt;victim_org_name&gt;@outlook[.]com. APT42 also browsed and downloaded files from the victim’s OneDrive to disk, likely to access files of interest. </span></li>
<li style="text-align:justify"><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">Using anonymized infrastructure</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> to interact with the victim’s environment, including ExpressVPN nodes, Cloudflare-hosted domains, and ephemeral VPS servers. </span></li>
</ul>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Despite the previously listed defense evasion techniques, Mandiant was able to attribute the cloud operations to APT42 based on the usage of domains overlapping with APT42 credential harvesting operations and the very specific Iran-related nature of intelligence collected by the actor. </span></p>
<h2 style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">APT42 Malware-Based Operations</span></h2>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Mandiant tracks several APT42 campaigns using custom malware. Most recently, Mandiant observed APT42 deploy two custom backdoors, TAMECAT and NICECURL. Both of these backdoors were delivered with decoy content (likely via spear phishing) and provide APT42 operators with initial access to the targets. The backdoors provide a flexible code-execution interface that may be used as a jumping point to deploy additional malware or to manually execute commands on the device.</span></p>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Mandiant estimates APT42 used these backdoors to target NGOs, </span><span style="vertical-align:baseline">government, or intergovernmental organizations around the world,</span><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> handling issues related to Iran and the Middle East, consistent with APT42 targeting profile.<br><br></span></p>

<tr>
<td style="vertical-align:middle;border:1px solid #000000;padding:16px">

<p style="text-align:center"><span style="vertical-align:baseline;color:#5f6368;display:block;font-size:16px;font-style:italic;margin-top:8px;width:100%">Table 1: APT42 Malware Families</span></p>
<h3 style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">NICECURL</span></h3>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">NICECURL is a backdoor written in VBScript that can download additional modules to be executed, including a datamining module, and it provides an arbitrary command execution interface. The backdoor’s accepted commands include "kill" to remove artifacts and end execution, "SetNewConfig" to set a new sleep value, and "Module" to download and execute additional files, potentially extending NICECURL's functionality. NICECURL communicates over HTTPS.</span></p>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">In January 2024, Mandiant observed a malicious LNK file downloading NICECURL and a PDF decoy that masqueraded as an Interview Feedback Form of the Harvard T.H. Chan School of Public Health (Figure 18). The decoy mentions an interviewee by the name of Daniel Serwer, possibly referring to the scholar and foreign policy researcher by the same name, affiliated with the Middle East Institute. It is noteworthy that Mandiant has no indication these entities were targeted or compromised, but merely spoofed by APT42 decoys.</span></p></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig18.max-900x900.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig18.max-900x900.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig18.max-900x900.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig18.max-900x900.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Figure 18: PDF decoy</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The LNK file onedrive-form.pdf.lnk (MD5: d5a05212f5931d50bb024567a2873642) is downloaded from hxxps://drive-file-share[.]site/OneDrive-Form.pdf.lnk. class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">According to the contents of the decoy file, the attack possibly happened in January or the beginning of February 2024 and targeted a victim located in Australia.</span></p>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Mandiant also observed a similarly named encrypted RAR file named “question_Empowering Women for Peace Gender Equality in Conflict Prevention and Resolution (6).rar” (MD5: 13aa118181ac6a202f0a64c0c7a61ce7). This RAR file shares the same name with the decoy PDF and likely targeted the same victim. </span></p>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">This infection chain was previously documented by </span><a href="https://www.volexity.com/blog/2024/02/13/charmingcypress-innovating-persistence/" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">Volexity</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline">.</span></p>
<h3 style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">TAMECAT </span></h3>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">In March 2024, Mandiant identified a sample of TAMECAT, a PowerShell toehold that can execute arbitrary PowerShell or C# content. TAMECAT is dropped by malicious macro documents, communicates with its command-and-control (C2) node via HTTP, and expects data from the C2 to be Base64 encoded. Mandiant previously observed TAMECAT used in a large-scale APT42 spear-phishing campaign targeting individuals or entities employed by or affiliated with NGOs, government, or intergovernmental organizations around the world.</span></p>
<h4 style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">TAMECAT Execution</span></h4>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Execution begins with a small VBScript downloader that leverages Windows Management Instrumentation (WMI) to query anti-virus products running on the victim's system. Depending on the script determining if Windows Defender is running, differing download commands and URLs are used.</span></p>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">If Windows Defender is running, the script will leverage conhost to execute a PowerShell command that uses Wget to download content at the following URL: hxxps://s3[.]tebi[.]io/icestorage/config/nconf.txt.</span></p>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">For all other cases, the script uses Cmd.exe to execute a Curl command that is similar to Curl commands used in the NICECURL execution chain previously described:<br><br></span></p>

<ul>
<li style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Downloads: hxxps://s3[.]tebi[.]io/icestorage/config/nconf.txt (MD5: 081419a484bbf99f278ce636d445b9d8)</span>

</ul>

</ul></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig21.max-1300x1300.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig21.max-1300x1300.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig21.max-1300x1300.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig21.max-1300x1300.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Figure 21: a2.vbs content</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The downloaded script, nconf.txt (MD5: 081419a484bbf99f278ce636d445b9d8), is a PowerShell script that contains an obfuscated and AES-encrypted TAMECAT backdoor. The script also downloads an additional PowerShell that is used to AES decrypt the embedded TAMECAT backdoor.</span></p>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">When downloading the AES decryption script, the following hard-coded User-agent string is used:</span></p>
<ul style="text-align:left">
<li><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Mozilla/5.0 (Windows NT 10.0; Win64; x64) AppleWebKit/537.36 (KHTML, like Gecko) Chrome/119.0.0.0 Safari/537.36</span></li>
</ul>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">It is noteworthy that the script contains a unique TAMECAT key value T2r0y1M1e1n1o0w1 that was used in a previously reported TAMECAT sample observed in June 2023 (MD5: dd2653a2543fa44eaeeff3ca82fe3513), further indicating the two samples belong to the same malware family. However, the unique value is not used in the script.</span></p>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The script stores the URL for the AES decryption script as a Base64 string where the first three characters are truncated and the remaining string is Base64 decoded: </span></p>
<ul style="text-align:left">
<li><strong style="vertical-align:baseline">pep</strong><span style="vertical-align:baseline">aHR0cHM6Ly9zMy50ZWJpLmlvL2ljZXN0b3JhZ2UvZGYzMnMudHh0</span>
<ul>
<li>Decodes to: hxxps://s3[.]tebi[.]io/icestorage/df32s.txt</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The script stored at this URL is df32s.txt (MD5: c3b9191f3a3c139ae886c0840709865e)</span></li>
</ul>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The response content is Base64 decoded and also further decoded using a routine that does the following:</span></p>
<ul style="text-align:left">
<li><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Inverts the bits of each byte within an array named $bytesOfRes</span></li>
<li><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Extracts the least significant byte (8 bits) from the inverted representation</span></li>
<li><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Converts the extracted byte back into a numerical byte value</span></li>
</ul>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Once decoded, the resulting PowerShell function resembles the following:</span></p></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig22.max-800x800.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig22.max-800x800.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig22.max-800x800.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig22.max-800x800.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Figure 22: Decoded df32s.txt</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The decoded script is a function that is mainly used to AES decrypt parameters that are passed to it. In addition, it defines global variables including a C2 domain, which are used by the TAMECAT backdoor that gets decrypted and executed.</span></p>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The following AES key and IV are used to decrypt content:</span></p>
<ul style="text-align:left">
<li><span style="vertical-align:baseline">AES Key: kNz0CXiP0wEQnhZXYbvraigXvRVYHk1B</span></li>
<li><span style="vertical-align:baseline">AES IV: 0T9r1y1M2e0N0o1w</span></li>
</ul>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The parent script uses the AES decrypt function to decode Base64, and AES decrypts the following string that is contained in the parent script:<br><br></span></p>
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">
<div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">

<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The TAMECAT backdoor makes an initial POST request to the globally defined C2 domain: hxxps://accurate-sprout-porpoise[.]glitch[.]me. </span></p>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The initial POST request contains information like the following, which are AES encrypted and Base64 encoded:<br><br></span></p>

</div></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The TAMECAT backdoor AES encrypts the content using the key kNz0CXiP0wEQnhZXYbvraigXvRVYHk1B and a randomly generated 16-character IV, generated from the string ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz. The randomly generated IV is added to the POST request in a header called Content-DPR. The AES key is not transmitted to the C2, so it is likely the same AES key is used for multiple victims. </span></p>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">If the response is successful, it is also expected to contain a header named Content-DPR, which is expected to house an IV used with the aforementioned AES key to decrypt the response data.</span></p>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The decrypted response data is split by the paragraph symbol (¶) into four values:</span></p>
<ul style="text-align:left">
<li><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Language</span></li>
<li><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Command</span></li>
<li><span style="vertical-align:baseline">ThreadName</span></li>
<li><span style="vertical-align:baseline">StartStop</span></li>
</ul>
<p style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The available commands appear mostly the same as previously identified TAMECAT samples:<br><br></span></p>

<h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Outlook and Implications</span></h2>
<p style="text-align:justify"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">APT42 has remained relatively focused on intelligence collection and targeting similar victimology, despite the Israel-Hamas war that has led other Iran-nexus actors to adapt by conducting disruptive, destructive, and hack-and-leak activities. </span></p>
<p style="text-align:justify"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">In addition to deploying custom implants on compromised devices, APT42 was also observed conducting extensive cloud operations. In cloud environments not vulnerable to implants, APT42 relies on social engineering to harvest credentials and collect intelligence of strategic interest to Iran. </span><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Credential abuse was also emphasized as a common initial access vector to cloud environments in the latest <a href="https://services.google.com/fh/files/misc/threat_horizons_report_h12024.pdf" rel="noopener" target="_blank">Google Cloud Threat Horizons </a></span><a href="https://services.google.com/fh/files/misc/threat_horizons_report_h12024.pdf" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">report</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline">.</span></p>
<p style="text-align:justify"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The methods deployed by APT42 leave a minimal footprint and might make the detection and mitigation of their activities more challenging for network defenders. The TTPs, IOCs, and provided rules included in this blog post may support detection and mitigation efforts.</span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">For Google Chronicle Enterpri</span><span style="vertical-align:baseline">se+ customers, Chronicle rules hav</span><span style="vertical-align:baseline">e been released to your </span><a href="https://cloud.google.com/chronicle/docs/preview/curated-detections/windows-threats-category"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">Emerging Threats</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> rule pack, and IOCs listed in this blog post are available for prioritization with </span><a href="https://cloud.google.com/chronicle/docs/detection"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">Applied Threat Intelligence</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline">. In addition, the IOCs listed in this blog post are blocked in </span><a href="https://safebrowsing.google.com/" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">Safe Browsing</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, protecting Google Chrome users, as well as other browsers.</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><h2 style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Indicators of Compromise (IOCs)</span></h2>
<p style="text-align:left">A <a href="https://www.virustotal.com/gui/collection/ebb39ba4f340314ef4f69394f0793fc1e995ee22a3786b3d3c5fc67a05552fd7/summary" rel="noopener" target="_blank">VirusTotal Collection featuring IOCs related to the APT42 activity</a> described in this post is now available for registered users.</p>

<h4 style="text-align:left"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">TAMECAT: YARA Rules</span></h4></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>rule M_APT_Backdoor_TAMECAT_2 {

style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eAPT42\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e, an Iranian state-sponsored cyber espionage actor, is using enhanced social engineering schemes to gain access to victim networks, including cloud environments. The actor is targeting Western and Middle Eastern NGOs, media organizations, academia, legal services and activists. Mandiant assesses APT42 operates on behalf of the Islamic Revolutionary Guard Corps Intelligence Organization (IRGC-IO).\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp style\u003d\"text-align:left\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eAPT42 was observed posing as journalists and event organizers to build trust with their victims through ongoing correspondence, and to deliver invitations to conferences or legitimate documents. These social engineering schemes enabled APT42 to harvest credentials and use them to gain initial access to cloud environments. Subsequently, the threat actor covertly exfiltrated data of strategic interest to Iran, while relying on built-in features and open-source tools to avoid detection.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp style\u003d\"text-align:left\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eIn addition to cloud operations, we also outline recent malware-based APT42 operations using two custom backdoors: NICECURL and TAMECAT. These backdoors are delivered via spear phishing, providing the attackers with initial access that might be used as a command execution interface or as a jumping point to deploy additional malware\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp style\u003d\"text-align:left\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eAPT42 targeting and missions are consistent with its assessed affiliation with the IRGC-IO, which is a part of the Iranian intelligence apparatus that is responsible for monitoring and preventing foreign threats to the Islamic Republic and domestic unrest.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp style\u003d\"text-align:left\"\u003e\u003cspan This often involves the use of typosquatted domains like washin\u003c/span\u003e\u003cstrong style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eq\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"text-align:left\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eAs an extension of their aforementioned credential harvesting operations, during 2022–2023, Mandiant observed However, since the initial enabler of these operations lies with credential harvesting, which APT42 conducts worldwide, it is possible the victimology is much wider.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp style\u003d\"text-align:left\"\u003e\u003cstrong style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eThese operations began with enhanced social engineering schemes to gain the initial access to victim networks\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e, often involving ongoing trust-building correspondence with the victim. Only then the desired credentials are acquired and multi-factor authentication (MFA) is bypassed, by serving a cloned website to capture the MFA token (which failed) and later by sending MFA push notifications to the victim (which succeeded). \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp style\u003d\"text-align:left\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eThese techniques have style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e, relying on built-in features and open-source tools to decrease their chances of being detected.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,[[[null,"\u003cp\u003eFigure 13: APT42 cloud operations attack methods to bypass MFA\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e: First, APT42 made attempts to acquire MFA tokens by using fake DUO pages, using subdomains with prefixes such as “api-\u0026lt;generated_id\u0026gt;[.]...” or using words like “duo”. When this failed, the actor sent authentication prompts to victims upon attempts to login, which succeeded. \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eIn a different intrusion, APT42 likely served a phishing site to capture the MFA token sent via SMS and leveraged the KMSI (Keep-me-Signed-In) feature to avoid reauthentication.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli style\u003d\"text-align:left\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eIn at least one instance, APT42 established a “persistent” login mechanism \u003c/span\u003e\u003cstrong style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eleveraging the Microsoft \u003c/strong\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/account-billing/using-app-passwords-with-apps-that-don-t-support-two-step-verification-5896ed9b-4263-e681-128a-a6f2979a7944\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003e\u003cstrong style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eapp password\u003c/strong\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cstrong style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e feature, likely in attempts to preserve ongoing access for future logins\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e without the need to re-verify their identity with MFA.\u003c/span\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli style\u003d\"text-align:left\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eMicrosoft’s app password feature is intended to be used with applications or devices that do not support MFA, and thus generates single-use passwords that do not require MFA. The feature is not enabled by default, and can be activated manually. Once this feature is enabled, any logged in user can create app passwords.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli style\u003d\"text-align:left\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eAPT42 leveraged the fact that the app password feature was enabled to create an app password for the compromised account. However, Mandiant has no indication that APT42 actually used it.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e\n\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003c/ul\u003e"]]],[null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,[[[null,"\u003cp\u003eFigure 16: Microsoft app password settings, exploited by APT42 for continuous MFA bypass\u003c/p\u003e"],["https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig16.max-500x500.png",null,null,"https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/untangling-apt42-fig16.max-500x500.png"],null,3]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli style\u003d\"text-align:left\"\u003e\u003cstrong style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eCovert exfiltration of data from the Microsoft 365 environment\u003c/strong\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e, including OneDrive documents, Outlook emails, and documents of potential interest to Iran including files pertaining its foreign affairs or the Persian Gulf region.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e\u003c/span\u003e\u003cstrong style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eThe M365 infiltration and data exfiltration included the following stages:\u003c/strong\u003e\n\u003cul\u003e\n\u003cli style\u003d\"text-align:left\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eLogging in to the victim email using Thunderbird email client, whose usage was approved by the attacker altering the user permissions.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/li\u003e\n\u003cli style\u003d\"text-align:left\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eLogging into the victim’s Citrix application and using Windows Remote Desktop Protocol (RDP). Most recently, Mandiant observed APT42 deploy two custom backdoors, TAMECAT and NICECURL. Both of these backdoors were delivered with decoy content (likely via spear phishing) and provide APT42 operators with initial access to the targets. content\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003c/td\u003e\n\u003c/tr\u003e\n\u003c/tbody\u003e\n\u003c/table\u003e\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003c/div\u003e\n\u003cp style\u003d\"text-align:center\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline;color:#5f6368;display:block;font-size:16px;font-style:italic;margin-top:8px;width:100%\"\u003eTable 1: APT42 Malware Families\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch3 style\u003d\"text-align:left\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eNICECURL\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h3\u003e\n\u003cp style\u003d\"text-align:left\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eNICECURL is a backdoor written in VBScript that can download additional modules to be executed, including a datamining module, and it provides an arbitrary command execution interface. The backdoor’s accepted commands include \"kill\" to remove artifacts and end execution, \"SetNewConfig\" to set a new sleep value, and \"Module\" to download and execute additional files, potentially extending NICECURL's functionality. NICECURL communicates over HTTPS.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp style\u003d\"text-align:left\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eIn January 2024, Mandiant observed a malicious LNK file downloading NICECURL and a PDF decoy that masqueraded as an Interview Feedback Form of the Harvard T.H. Chan School of Public Health (Figure 18).
